The GT has two basis functions:
1. **A²** (polynomial)
2. **sin(log(A + 1))** (a transcendental function)

The key question is: can any candidate produce `sin(log(A+1))`?

Let me scan through all candidates looking for:
- `sin(...)` terms
- `log(...)` terms
- Candidates with `t` dependence that can't be zeroed out

**Candidates with sin():** 58, 73, 76

**Candidate 58:** `A²c0 + Ac1/(A+c2) + c3*sin(A*c4+c5) + c6/(A*c7+c2)`
- Has `sin(A*c4 + c5)` which is `sin(linear in A)`. The GT needs `sin(log(A+1))`. These are fundamentally different functions — `sin(linear)` is periodic, `sin(log(A+1))` is not periodic in the usual sense. **No match.**

**Candidate 73:** `A²c0 + Ac1/(Ac2+c3) + c4*sin(Ac5+c6) + c7/(Ac2+c3)`
- Same issue: `sin(linear in A)` ≠ `sin(log(A+1))`. **No match.**

**Candidate 76:** `A²c0 + Ac1 + c2*sin(Ac3+c4) + c5*t/(c6+c7*exp(c8*t)) + c9/A`
- Again `sin(linear in A)`. **No match.**

**Candidates with log():** 1, 41, 67, 72

**Candidate 1:** `Ac0/(Ac1+c2) + c3*log(Ac4+1) + c5*t/(c6+c7*exp(c8*t)) + c9`
- Has `log(A*c4+1)` but needs `sin(log(A+1))`. `log` alone ≠ `sin(log(...))`. **No match.**

**Candidate 41:** `A²c0 + Ac1/(Ac2+c3) + c4*log(Ac5+1) + c6/(Ac2+c3)`
- Has `log(...)` but not `sin(log(...))`. **No match.**

**Candidate 67:** `A²c0 + Ac1 + c2*t/(c3+c4*exp(c5*t)) + c6*log(Ac7+1) + c8/A`
- Has `log(...)` but not `sin(log(...))`. **No match.**

**Candidate 72:** `Ac0/(Ac1+c2) + c3*log(Ac4+1) + c5*t/(c6+c7*exp(c8*t)) + c9/(Ac1+c2)`
- Has `log(...)` but not `sin(log(...))`. **No match.**

**All other candidates** are combinations of:
- Polynomials in A
- Rational functions A/(A*c+c)
- Exponentials exp(A*c)
- Some have t-dependence (which could potentially be zeroed)

None of these can produce `sin(log(A+1))`. The function `sin(log(A+1))` is a transcendental function that cannot be expressed as any finite combination of polynomials, rational functions, and exponentials. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, no combination of {polynomials, rational functions, exp(A*c)} can equal `sin(log(A+1))`.

Since the GT requires `sin(log(A+1))` and no candidate contains this basis function (or any composition that could produce it), no candidate can match.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

The GT consists of two basis functions:
1. `A²` (polynomial term)
2. `sin(log(A + 1))` (a transcendental function)

The key question is: can any combination of rational functions and exponentials exactly reproduce `sin(log(A+1))`?

**Critical observation:** `sin(log(A+1))` is a highly specific transcendental function. It cannot be represented by:
- Rational functions of A (polynomials divided by polynomials)
- Exponential functions like `exp(A*c)`
- Products of the above
- `log(A*c + 1)` alone (without sin)
